## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task models acceleration in a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt is determined by nonlinear restoring forces (functions of x), damping (functions of v), and possibly periodic driving (functions of t). Classical nonlinear oscillator models like Duffing, Van der Pol, and driven pendulum are the primary candidates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped linear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven damped Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven Duffing oscillator)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v (sinusoidal restoring + damping)
- Driven damped pendulum: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven pendulum)
- Quadratic-cubic restoring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear potential)
- Nonlinear damping with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * x**2 + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (position-dependent damping with drive)
- Coulomb-like friction: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) indicate symmetric potential wells; even powers (x²) indicate asymmetric potentials
- Position-dependent damping coefficient like (1 - x²)*v is characteristic of self-excited oscillators (Van der Pol type)
- Sinusoidal dependence on position sin(c*x) suggests a periodic potential or pendulum-like geometry
- Cosine or sine functions of time indicate external periodic driving forces
- Products of x and v terms (e.g., x²*v) indicate energy-dependent or amplitude-dependent dissipation
- Cubic position terms x³ with opposite sign to linear term x indicate a double-well (Duffing) potential
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or monotonically dissipated
- Mixed polynomial terms in x with alternating signs suggest Taylor expansion of a transcendental restoring force like sin(x)
